HOME-CONFIGURATION()                                                                                                                        HOME-CONFIGURATION()

NNAAMMEE
       home-configuration.nix - Home Manager configuration specification

DDEESSCCRRIIPPTTIIOONN
       The file ~/.config/nixpkgs/home.nix contains the declarative specification of your Home Manager configuration. The command hhoommee--mmaannaaggeerr takes this file
       and realises the user environment configuration specified therein.

OOPPTTIIOONNSS

       hhoommee..sseessssiioonnVVaarriiaabblleess
           Environment variables to always set at login.

           The values may refer to other environment variables using POSIX.2 style variable references. For example, a variable _p_a_r_a_m_e_t_e_r may be referenced as
           $parameter or ${parameter}. A default value foo may be given as per ${parameter:-foo} and, similarly, an alternate value bar can be given as per
           ${parameter:+bar}.

           Note, these variables may be set in any order so no session variable may have a runtime dependency on another session variable. In particular code
           like

                 home.sessionVariables = {
                   FOO = "Hello";
                   BAR = "$FOO World!";
                 };

           may not work as expected. If you need to reference another session variable, then do so inside Nix instead. The above example then becomes

                 home.sessionVariables = {
                   FOO = "Hello";
                   BAR = "${config.home.sessionVariables.FOO} World!";
                 };

           _T_y_p_e_: attribute set

           _D_e_f_a_u_l_t_: { }

           _E_x_a_m_p_l_e_: { EDITOR = "emacs"; GS_OPTIONS = "-sPAPERSIZE=a4"; }

           _D_e_c_l_a_r_e_d _b_y_:
               <<hhoommee--mmaannaaggeerr//mmoodduulleess//hhoommee--eennvviirroonnmmeenntt..nniixx>>

           How unread and relevant news should be presented when running hhoommee--mmaannaaggeerr bbuuiilldd and hhoommee--mmaannaaggeerr sswwiittcchh.

           silent

               The number of unread and relevant news entries will be printed to standard output. The hhoommee--mmaannaaggeerr nneewwss command can later be used to view the
               entries.

               A pager showing unread news entries is opened.
